The Health Information Portal is a one-stop shop facilitating access to population health and health care data, information and expertise in Europe. The aim of the Health Information Portal is to provide access to population health and healthcare data across Europe. The portal is the gateway for researcher and policy maker to make use of the service of the Research Infrastructure on Population Health Information (PHIRI). The Health Information Portal contains catalogue for Data sources, National and European projects, Research Infrastructures, capacity building activities, and COVID-19 related resource that help researcher to find and access population health information in a timely manner. An overview to the data model and metadata element of specific module of the Health Information Portal can be accessed here. Help u providing complete and accurate health information: register and start contributing to this portal FAIR catalogue The development make use of standard a given by the FAIR principle (Findable, Accessible, Interoperable, and Reusable). The portal now offer a FAIR catalogue with overview of COVID-19 population health data sources, study and capacity building excercises. The essential actor to provide the necessary information to feed the portal are the network of the National Nodes (NN), based on the Joint Action on Health Information (InfAct) framework The portal wa developed a part of the activity of the Joint Action on Health Information () a a cornerstone of the Distributed Infrastructure on Population Health (). The Population Health Information Research Infrastructure () is expanding the reach of the portal to also include population health information, data and expertise related to COVID-19. The Health Information Portal is a one-stop shop facilitating access to population health and health care data, information and expertise in Europe. The aim of the Health Information Portal is to provide access to population health and healthcare data across Europe. The portal is the gateway for researcher and policy maker to make use of the service of the Research Infrastructure on Population Health Information (). The Health Information Portal contains catalogue for Data sources, National and European projects, Research Infrastructures, capacity building activities, and COVID-19 related resource that help researcher to find and access population health information in a timely manner. An overview to the data model and metadata element of specific module of the Health Information Portal can be accessed . The Portal provides information on: Based on partner and users' feedback, the Portal is constantly updated and improved to provide the researcher and policy maker in Europe with key population health information for their work and research. PHIRIallows for better coordinated European effort across national and European stakeholder to generate the best COVID-19 population health knowledge. In doing so, PHIRI is laying the foundationto buildaResearch Infrastructure on Population Healthto be used to overcome future crisis andensurethe sustainability of the project. The intent is to support research across Europe through the identification, access, assessment and reuse of population health and non-health data to underpin public health policy decisions. InfAct The Joint Action on Health InformationInfAct(Information for Action!)is a 36months (plus extension of 3 months) project funded by the European Commission.It built on theand other initiative in health information. The project wa launched in March2018 and it ended in May 2022. It included 40partners in 28 EUand associated countries. Through country collaboration, InfAct streamlined health information activity across Europe. It laid the foundation to build a sustainable and solid infrastructure on EU health information and strengthens it core element based on capacity building, health information tool and political support. Country InternationalCountry outside EuropeAlbaniaAndorraArmeniaAustriaAzerbaijanBelarusBelgiumBosnia and HerzegovinaBulgariaCroatiaCyprusCzech RepublicDenmarkEstoniaFinlandFranceGeorgiaGermanyGreeceHungaryIcelandIrelandItalyKazakhstanKosovoLatviaLiechtensteinLithuaniaLuxembourgMaltaMoldovaMonacoMontenegroNetherlandsNorth MacedoniaNorwayPolandPortugalRomaniaRussiaSan MarinoSerbiaSlovakiaSloveniaSpainSwedenSwitzerlandTurkeyUkraineUnited KingdomVatican City Breadcrumb - - Health Information Portal - API Health Information Portal - API This guide will explain what an API is and how you can use the service to query the knowledge graph database linked with the Health Information Portal website. What kind of information can be harvested? The Health Information Portal API provides comprehensive, open access to an extensive array of catalogue and data source information showcased on the Health Information Portal Website. It furnishes a plethora of detailed metadata in a machine-readable format, adhering to the DCAT-AP metadata standard, which includes essential metadata element such a dataset titles, comprehensive descriptions, languages, geographic locations, landing pages, publishers, and beyond. This meticulously structured approach guarantee effortless integration and streamlined processing by automated frameworks, thus enhancing the depth of understanding and the contextual relevance of each dataset. Such structured metadata facilitates not only a deeper comprehension of the datasets' core attribute but also amplifies their accessibility and usability, ensuring that researchers, healthcare professionals, and policy maker can leverage this information effectively to advance public health initiative and outcomes. What is an API? An API, short for Application Programming Interface, act a a digital intermediary that allows different computer program to communicate and share data. It defines the rule and command for software application to request and exchange information. APIs enable apps to interact with services, creating seamless and integrated experiences. In essence, APIs make our digital world more interconnected, allowing device and software to work together and share data, enhancing their functionality. How doe it work? The Health Information Portal Website is regularly harvested by a Fair Data Point instance to store all it content into a knowledge graph database (TripleStore) using RDF technology and international DCAT-AP metadata standard. This aligns the Health Information Portal with semantic technologies, making it content Findable, Accessible, Interoperable, and Reusable (FAIR) by machines. The Fair Data Point API is an HATEOAS (Hypertext a the Engine of Application State) RESTful API. HATEOAS is a fundamental principle in RESTful API design that encourages the use of hypermedia to drive the application's state. In a HATEOAS-enabled REST API, client interact with resource and navigate the API by following link provided by the server. How to retrieve information using the API? The command below describes how to query the Fair Data Point server through it API to retrieve the content of a metadata record related to the Health Information Portal website. Although retrieving metadata is open for GET request without authorization, metadata record can't be updated or created without authorization. The Swagger interface of the Fair Data Point server for the Health Information Portal is available: Base URL: Example of UUID: HTTP method: GET The supported serialization of the RDF document: Turtle: text/turtle N3: text/n3 RDF/XML: application/rdf+xml JSON-LD: application/ld+json In the following example, we retrieve a Dataset resource by issuing a GET request to the /dataset prefix followed by it identifier (a UUID). Curl command curl -H "Accept: text/turtle" https://fair.healthinformationportal.eu/dataset/a8832b77-2075-400a-93b2-35d974261f80 Python command: import request uri = https://fair.healthinformationportal.eu/dataset/a8832b77-2075-400a-93b2-35d974261f80 header = {'Accept': 'text/turtle'} re = requests.get(url=uri, headers=headers) print(res.text) These command will harvest the RDF metadata record corresponding to the UUID and output it following a turtle serialization. Country InternationalCountry outside EuropeAlbaniaAndorraArmeniaAustriaAzerbaijanBelarusBelgiumBosnia and HerzegovinaBulgariaCroatiaCyprusCzech RepublicDenmarkEstoniaFinlandFranceGeorgiaGermanyGreeceHungaryIcelandIrelandItalyKazakhstanKosovoLatviaLiechtensteinLithuaniaLuxembourgMaltaMoldovaMonacoMontenegroNetherlandsNorth MacedoniaNorwayPolandPortugalRomaniaRussiaSan MarinoSerbiaSlovakiaSloveniaSpainSwedenSwitzerlandTurkeyUkraineUnited KingdomVatican City Breadcrumb - Rapid Exchange Forum Rapid Exchange Forum Within PHIRI,, aRapid Exchange Forum (REF) is organized regularly every two week or a needed, addressing urgent question and current development in population health during the COVID-19 pandemic and beyond. In this one hour meeting, the participant belonging to European public health institutes, Ministries of Health, research institution and university a well a EU-level stakeholder answer question and discus experience from their own country related to the COVID-19 pandemic and other population health issue that require rapid responses. Each meeting is organized around a topic or set of topic of timely relevance to the participating countries, and answer to the question are shared during the meeting a well a in writing immediately before or after the meetings. This allows arapid exchange of information across countriesto learn from each others challenge and best practices, and compare e.g. vaccination-, testing-, and communication strategies, reaction to new virus variants, mortality indicators, long-term pandemic monitoring and surveillance, and impact evaluation of the pandemic. The answer to question discussed during the REF meeting are uploaded to the Health Information Portal at the latest by the end of the week in which each meeting take place. Please use the search function below to browse the content of previous REF meetings. In order to search for an exact phrase, you can utilize quotation mark around your search term. Search topic and question Free keywords Topics Title Question Date Document(s) Trust in exchange of data for secondary use purpose 11-Mar-2024 Covid infection in vaccinated people in autumn/winter 12-Feb-2024 Human Respiratory Syncytial Virus (RSV) and hospitalisation rate in child 15-Jan-2024 Prevalence of sexually transmitted infection in Europe Currently there is a systematic review conducted on the prevalence of 4 sexually transmitted infection in Europe: chlamydia, gonorrhoea, syphilis and trichomoniasis. We are conducting extensive literature search in bibliographic database but are also interested in grey literature.We would be very grateful if you could: indicate to u any report on the prevalence of any of the 4 STIs in your country, published/conducted within the last 10 years, that ha not been published in a peer-reviewed journal and/or forward our request to expert in the field in your country! (The focus of this request is on grey literature, but please dont hesitate to also indicate relevant peer-reviewed literature, especially recent publications.) Please note that for this review we are not interested in incidence estimate derived from routine surveillance (i.e., number of case notification per national/regional population), but only in prevalence estimate derived from a study where the total population of tested individual is known and described. 18-Dec-2023 Covid-19 combined vaccination In country where Covid-19 is vaccinated combined with another immunization, e.g. against influenza, wa there a (remarkable) increase of Covid-19 vaccinations? What could have caused this increase, what are the possible reasons?Are there any learning with such a system? Please share your experiences. 20-Nov-2023 Covid-19 measure Update per October 2023 The following Y/N questions, asked in a live poll during the meeting, are intended to be displayed on the Health Information Portal: A. Please give examples. 11-Sep-2023 Biosimilar medicine Interchangeability: Does your country have a legal arrangement in place such that once a biosimilar is approved in the EU (or through some other mechanism) it is interchangeable, which mean the biosimilar can be used instead of it reference product (or vice versa) or one biosimilar can be replaced with another biosimilar of the same reference product? If so, please briefly describe the arrangement? (i.e., only reimburse the preferred biosimilar) If so, doe the pharmacist/dispenser receive training or specific payment from the Government or insurer? Has the above approach encountered criticism in your country? The relevant stakeholder may include, for example, the national statistical office, the national public health institutes, representative from ministry of health, research and/or science, and others. In addition, the National Nodes may function a a discussion and advisory forum in matter of health data and information both for national or international matters. Information regarding whether or not a country ha a National Node established in the PHIRI network, is available on the main page of each country, which is reachable through the map below. Gesundheit sterreich GmbH Nemzeti Egszsgbiztostsi Alapkezel Aim of the network/project EURIPID is a voluntary, non-profit collaboration of the European pricing and reimbursement authority for the mutual sharing of information regarding pharmaceutical pricing policy and price of medicinal products. Its main objective is to make pricing procedure and price of pharmaceutical more transparent in Europe. In order to do so, the EURIPID Collaboration set up and maintains a technical tool, the EURIPID database. The EURIPID database is a comprehensive, continuously maintained, easy-to-use online database of price of reimbursed pharmaceuticals. The database is a resource tool for member of the EURIPID Collaboration and exclusively accessiblee for the national competent authority of it participating country and the service of the European Commission. The EURIPID Collaboration consists of (1) founding members, (2) partners, (3) associated partner and (4) the European Commission (EC). Regarding it governance structure, the EURIPID Collaboration ha a Board of Participants and an Executive Committee. The Board of Participants includes one delegate per country and a representative of the EC. The Executive Committee ha six members: the delegate of the two founders, three delegate of the Board of Participants and one representative of the EC. The EURIPID Collaboration is currently funded by an annual contribution fee of the participant and for defined task (e.g. the public website) and deliverable two grant of the European Commission awarded in 2019 and 2023. Topics Health system Health resource and activity Pharmaceutical sale & consumption Free keywords price volume managed entry agreement pricing system Countries: Acronym PERISCOPE Aim of the network/project The COVID-19 pandemic ha shown that effective assessment and response requires diverse data from various disciplines. Evaluating the true impact of the outbreak requires data and statistical analysis that are not always readily available. The EU-funded PERISCOPE project aim to conduct in-depth multidisciplinary research to evaluate and better inform Europes response to the pandemic. It doe so by assessing the outbreak impact while taking policy measure a well a epidemiological, health, socioeconomic impact into account. The main goal of the project is to uncover the real impact of the pandemic by providing a wealth of data and statistical information, promoting evidence-based policymaking while informing effective outbreak response. Topics Policy Health status Morbidity/disability Communicable disease Covid-19 Free keywords governance pandemic virology coronaviruses Acronym HEPA Europe Aim of the network/project The mission of HEPA Europe is to provide a forum for the advancement of health-enhancing physical activity (HEPA) research, policy and practice for better health and well-being across the WHO European Region. HEPA Europe membership is open to organization and institution active at the regional, national or subnational level, who are willing to contribute to the goal and objective of the network. Topics Determinants of health Individual characteristic and behaviour Behaviours Physical activity Acronym SYNCHROS Aim of the network/project The SYNCHROS-project started Jan. 1st, 2019 and end June 30th, 2022. The work towards the goal of Coordination and Support for Synchronising Cohorts and Population Surveys in Europe and worldwide is structured by 8 work package and the following three phases. Free keywords patient Clinical trial Population cohort Acronym ReCODID Aim of the network/project The RECODID project will develop an equitable, accessible, and sustainable model for the storage, curation, and analysis of clinical-epidemiological and high-dimensional sample data collected by infectious disease cohort in low-and-middle-income country (LMIC). Free keywords Clinical research Barriers Infectious disease Metadata Acronym HBM4EU Aim of the network/project HBM4EU is coordinating and advancing human biomonitoring in Europe and so provide better evidence of the actual exposure of citizen to chemicals. In addition, we provide a robust interpretation of human biomonitoring data and the possible impact of chemical exposure on human health, using the most up to date scientific tools. HBM4EU partner effectively communicates result to policy makers, ensuring their exploitation in the design of new chemical policy and the evaluation of existing measures. This initiative contributes directly to the improvement of health and well-being for all citizens, by investigating how exposure to chemical affect the health of different vulnerable groups, such a child and pregnant women, a well a of highly exposed group like workers. Data used and produced under HBM4EU will be made accessible via. IPCHEM is the European Commissions reference access point for searching, accessing and retrieving chemical occurrence data collected and managed in Europe. Topics Determinants of health Physical and social environment Physical environment Free keywords Biomonitoring Chemical exposure Vulnerable population Acronym EU-RESPONSE Aim of the network/project The overall objective of this 5-year project is to build a multinational, adaptive European COVID-19 and emerging infectious disease trial network, based on existing initiatives, experience and expertise, allowing European expansion of DisCoVeRy and the establishment of a COVID-19 adaptive platform trial. Topics Health system Health system performance Health system Health resource and activity Pharmaceutical sale & consumption Free keywords COVID-19 Clinical trial Emerging infectious disease Acronym ORCHESTRA Aim of the network/project ORCHESTRA is a three-year international research project aimed at tackling the coronavirus pandemic, led by the University of Verona and involving 26 partner (extending to a wider network of 37 partners) from 15 countries: Argentina, Belgium, Brazil, Congo, France, Gabon, Germany, India, Italy, Luxemburg, Netherlands, Romania, Slovakia, Spain, Venezuela. The project is funded by theEuropean Unions Horizon 2020 research and innovation programmeunder theERAvsCORONAAction Plan which wa developed jointly by Commission service and national authorities. Objectives to develop evidence-based recommendation for effective prevention, protection and optimized treatment of COVID-19 patient (including long-term consequences) with a special focus on at risk population, including healthcare worker and fragile individual to ass impact of environmental factors, socio-economic determinants, lifestyle and confinement measure on the spread of COVID-19 to provide knowledge on the efficacy of vaccine against SARS-CoV-2 to provide a model for responsiveness for future pandemic outbreaks. Institute)sterreichische Agentur fr Gesundheit und Ernhrungssicherheit sterreichische Gesellschaft fr Public Healthsterreichische Sozialversicherungstav pro pi o matku a dt Aim of the network/project BBMRI-ERIC is a European research infrastructure for biobanking. BBMRI brings together all the main player from the biobanking field researchers, biobankers, industry, and patient to boost biomedical research. To that end, it offer quality management services, support with ethical, legal and societal issues, and a number of online tool and software solutions. Ultimately, the goal of BBMRI is to make new treatment possible. Aim of the network/project Health-RIisthe Dutch national initiative tofacilitate and stimulate an integrated health data infrastructure accessible for researchers, citizens, care provider and industry.Itwill enable optimal use of health data, sample and images, a learning healthcare system and accelerate personalized health. Topics Health system Health status Acronym CESSDA Leading institute CESSDA Main Office Aim of the network/project CESSDA provides large-scale, integrated and sustainable data service to the social sciences. It brings together social science data archive across Europe, with the aim of promoting the result of social science research and supporting national and international research and cooperation. Countries: Acronym Euro Bioimaging Aim of the network/project Euro-BioImaging is the Europeanlandmarkresearch infrastructure for biological and biomedical imaging a recognised by the European Strategy Forum on Research Infrastructures (ESFRI). Through Euro-BioImaging, life scientist can access imaging instruments, expertise, training opportunity and data management service that they might not find at their home institution or among their collaboration partners. All scientists, regardless of their affiliation, area of expertise or field of activity can benefit from these pan-European open access services, which are provided with high quality standard by leading imaging facilities. Euro-BioImaging Mission To provide access, service and training to state-of-the-art imaging technology for all life scientist in Europe and beyond To foster the liaison and cooperation of all it stakeholder (including scientists, industry, national and European authorities) Topics Determinants of health Individual characteristic and behaviour Individual characteristic Free keywords Imaging Bio-imaging medical imaging screening Countries: Acronym ELIXIR Leading institute ELIXIR Hub Aim of the network/project The goal of ELIXIR is to coordinate these resource so that they form a single infrastructure.This infrastructure make it easier for scientist to find and share data, exchange expertise, and agree on best practices. Ultimately, it will help them gain new insight into how living organism work. Topics Determinants of health Individual characteristic and behaviour Individual characteristic Free keywords chemical biology enzymes, protein molecular and cellular structure computing Interoperability Rare disease Countries: Acronym EATRIS Aim of the network/project EATRIS is the European infrastructure for translational medicine. We bring together resource and service for research community to translate scientific discovery into benefit for patients. We provide access to a vast array of pre-clinical and clinical expertise and facility that are available within 100+ top-tier academic centre across Europe. We focus on improving and optimising preclinical and early clinical development of drugs, vaccine and diagnostics. Our research infrastructure offer a broad range ofresearch servicesfor bothacademiaand industry across various research fields.In addition, we work with public funding agencies, charity and policy maker with tailored action to help improve the translational research and innovation ecosystem. Topics Determinants of health Individual characteristic and behaviour Individual characteristic Free keywords Biomarkers Vaccines Imaging Translational medicine Acronym ECRIN Leading institute ECRIN European Clinical Research Infrastructure Network Aim of the network/project ECRIN's vision is to generate scientific evidence to optimise medical practice. To achieve this vision, ECRIN support the conduct of multinational clinical research in Europe (i.e. it vision). By managing and supporting clinical trial across borders, connecting networks, and advising and implementing policy, ECRIN advance knowledge flow, competitiveness and integration in European clinical research. ECRIN's value include healthcare optimisation, health innovation, patient involvement, scientific excellence, ethics, transparency, data sharing, high-quality data, not-for-profit focus, and international cooperation. We bring together all the main player from the biobanking field researchers, biobankers, industry, and patient to boost biomedical research. To that end, we offer quality management services, support with ethical, legal and societal issues, and a number of online tool and software solution for biobankers and researchers. Ultimately, our goal is to make new treatment possible. Institute)sterreichische Agentur fr Gesundheit und Ernhrungssicherheit sterreichische Gesellschaft fr Public Healthsterreichische Sozialversicherungstav pro pi o matku a dt Acronym NHS England Aim of the network/project Our purpose is to lead the NHS in England to deliver high-quality service for all. We do this by ensuring that the healthcare workforce ha the right numbers, skills, value and behaviour to support the delivery of excellent healthcare and health improvement to patient and the public.; a once-in-a-generation opportunity to put staffing on a sustainable footing and improve patient care. We work with the wider NHS and our partner to optimise the use of digital technology, research and innovation, and to deliver value for money and increased productivity and efficiency. We are responsible for running the vital national IT system which support health and social care, and the collection, analysis, publication and dissemination of data generated by health and social care service to improve outcome for patients. The establishment of integrated care board within integrated care systems, which are made up of public service that provide health and care, mean that NHS England is changing the way it work to best support and empower local system partner to deliver on their responsibilities. Oursets out how we are supporting system and provider to lead locally to improve the health of the population, improve the quality of patient care, tackle inequality and deliver care more efficiently. It describes our six longer-term aims: Longer healthy life expectancy. Excellent quality, safety and outcomes. Excellent access and experience. Equity of healthy life expectancy, quality, safety, outcomes, access and experience. Value for taxpayer money. Support to society, the economy and environment. Acronym WDF Aim of the network/project WDF is a leading funder of diabetes prevention and care project in low- and middle-income countries. The World Diabetes Foundation wa founded in 2002 a an independent foundation by Novo Nordisk A/S, and today is a leading global funder of diabetes prevention and care project in low- and middle-income countries. Our vision: We alleviate human suffering related to diabetes among those in greatest need. Our mission: We create partnership to assist people with diabetes and those at risk, acting a a catalyst to help others do more We link people and resource to educate and advocate globally and provide care locally Our priority is to support the poorest of the poor We empower local community to achieve sustainable solution and yield replicable model We encourage innovative strategy to prevent diabetes and it consequence Acronym NCD Alliance Aim of the network/project The mission of the NCD Alliance is to unite civil society and drive action on noncommunicable disease (NCD) prevention and care, leaving no one behind. NCDA brings together 300 member in 81 countries, including a network of 66 national and regional NCD alliances, to form a respected, united and credible global civil society movement. Our community includes member organisation addressing NCDs and their risk factors, national and regional NCD alliance and people living with NCDs. Acronym ASPHER Aim of the network/project The Association of Schools of Public Health in the European Region (ASPHER) is the key independent European organisation dedicated to improving and protecting the public health by strengthening education and training of public health professional for both practice and research. The main function of the Association are: To support theprofessionalisation of the public health workforcein Europe, whilst respecting the diversity of national and regional context in which each school of public health operates, and thus: To sustaincapacity building in public health, so that it balance with national and European population health challenge and threats, and is supported by best standard of public health education and training, scientific research, and practice. The general objective of ASPHER are: To sustain, in theory and practice,member schoolsin achieving their mission of education, training, scientific research and service; To develop model forpublic health education and trainingat all academic and professional levels, and the interaction of education and training with population health, health system and services; To promote structured process of sharingevidence-based public healthmodels of innovation and good practice; To buildcoalitionswith other programme and public health organisation whose mission is to improve public health, specifically in an effort to put forth high standard in and strengthen public health education and training and to improve the quality of the public health workforce in Europe and it competitiveness globally. ASPHER is a membership organisation of institutions, spread across EU and wider across WHO European Region, which are collectively concerned with the education and training, and professionalism, of those entering and working within the public health workforce. It promotes activity which foster exchange of information and best practice amongst it member in an effort to achieve high standard of public health education and training across Europe. Acronym UMU Aim of the network/project Formally established in 1965, Ume University is a comprehensive university covering research and education in medicine, science and technology, social sciences, art and humanities, and educational sciences. Our cohesive campus environment enables a dynamic and open culture with a strong sense of community. As a knowledge-driven organisation, Ume University is striving to provide student and staff with unique opportunity for learning and development whilst simultaneously serving society with new knowledge and creative citizens. Acronym AECC Aim of the network/project To alleviate and prevent, a far a possible, the suffering caused by cancer in people, wherever they live and whatever their personal circumstances. Acronym FOPH Aim of the network/project Federal Office of Public Health Schwarzenburgstrasse 157 3003 Bern, Switzerland pss2023@bag.admin.ch Acronym UNICEF Aim of the network/project UNICEF work in over 190 country and territory to save childrens lives, to defend their rights, and to help them fulfil their potential, from early childhood through adolescence. Acronym DG HERA Aim of the network/project The Health Emergency Preparedness and Response (HERA) department mission is to prevent, detect, and rapidly respond to health emergencies. HERA, created in the aftermath of the COVID-19 pandemic, will anticipate threat and potential health crises, through intelligence gathering and building the necessary response capacities. When an emergency hits, HERA will ensure the development, production and distribution of medicines, vaccine and other medical countermeasure such a glove and mask that were often lacking during the first phase of the response to the COVID-19 pandemic. HERA is a key pillar of the European Health Union announced by President von der Leyen in herand will fill a gap in the EU's health emergency response and preparedness. HERA wa launched a a new European Commission Directorate-General on 16 September 2021. Research Network In the past years, criminal and terrorist have been using method for concealing incriminating information in digital medium file such a images, video, audio, and text files. The main objective of UNCOVER is to develop innovative technology for detecting hidden information (steganalysis) and to increase the technological autonomy of Law Enforcement Agencies (LEAs) in the field of digital medium steganalysis. Network website Acronym DELIVER Aim of the Research Network The digital transformation of health is dramatically requesting the use of digital technology in European health care systems. HCPs are core in accelerating the digital transformation of health. The EU Joint Action Health Workforce Planning and Forecasting state digital skill are an important future skill for healthcare workers. Heath care professional will require knowledge on how to transfer their health-related skill to the new digitalised healthcare paradigm. Network website Acronym TEPHINET Leading institute Task Force for Global Health Aim of the Research Network TEPHINET aim to improve Field Epidemiology Training Programs, thereby facilitating their integration into every country in the world and ensuring sustainability and long-term funding. Free keywords Epidemiology Training Public health Workforce Network website Countries: Acronym EBoDN Aim of the Research Network What are the most relevant disease in a country? Which risk factor are the strongest contributor to disease and death? How is the impact of different disease evolving over time, and how doe it compare between country and within subnational units? As the need for prioritising the use of available resource constantly increases, a timely, sound and comprehensive answer to these fundamental question is more than ever needed to inform public health decision making. This includes policy and action for promoting child safety, consumer safety, safety for seniors, safety of vulnerable road users, safety in sport and the prevention of violence and self harm. Network website Countries: Acronym Euro-Peristat Leading institute INSTITUT NATIONAL DE LA SANTE ET DE LA RECHERCHE MEDICALE Aim of the Research Network The objective of the Euro-Peristat Network is to establish a high quality, innovative, internationally recognized and sustainable European perinatal information system. This system's goal is to produce data and analysis on a regular basis for use by national, European and international stakeholder who make decision about the health and health care of pregnant woman and newborns. Network website Countries: Acronym SHARE Aim of the Research Network The Survey of Health, Ageing and Retirement in Europe (SHARE) is a research infrastructure for studying the effect of health, social, economic and environmental policy over the life-course of European citizen and beyond. From 2004 until today, 530,000 in-depth interview with 140,000 people aged 50 or older from 28 European country and Israel have been conducted. Country InternationalCountry outside EuropeAlbaniaAndorraArmeniaAustriaAzerbaijanBelarusBelgiumBosnia and HerzegovinaBulgariaCroatiaCyprusCzech RepublicDenmarkEstoniaFinlandFranceGeorgiaGermanyGreeceHungaryIcelandIrelandItalyKazakhstanKosovoLatviaLiechtensteinLithuaniaLuxembourgMaltaMoldovaMonacoMontenegroNetherlandsNorth MacedoniaNorwayPolandPortugalRomaniaRussiaSan MarinoSerbiaSlovakiaSloveniaSpainSwedenSwitzerlandTurkeyUkraineUnited KingdomVatican City Breadcrumb - ECHI: European Core Health Indicators ECHI: European Core Health Indicators What isECHI? The European Core (formerly: Community) Health Indicators (ECHI)initiative started in 1998 a a project responding to the European Commission (EC)s call to establish ashortlist of public health indicator which would serve a the core of a European public health monitoring system. The first version of theECHIshortlist wa approved by theECand theEUMember States(MS)in 2005. In 2008, theECand theEUMS began putting the indicator into practice. The current shortlist contains 88 indicatorsgrouped into five main chaptersand mapped to 17 (non-exclusive) policy areas.Currently, 67 have been put into practice (implemented). TheECHIwork ha been coordinated through a series offiveECfunded projects:ECHI-I,ECHI-II,ECHIM,JAECHIM. TheBRIDGE Health project(2015-2018)and the Joint Action on Health Information (2018-2021) have suggested improvement to the ECHI. TheECHIIndicators derive their data from a variety of sources, including theEU's statistical office (Eurostat), the World Health Organisations European Health for all database (HFA-DB), the Health Statistics database of the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD) and several topic-specific databases. ECHI DOCUMENTATION Original ECHI report ECHI related report ) ECHIdata tool TheEuropean Commission Directorate of Health and Food SafetyDG SANTEestablished agraphic tool and an interactive application to present relevant and comparable information on health at European level, the. Country InternationalCountry outside EuropeAlbaniaAndorraArmeniaAustriaAzerbaijanBelarusBelgiumBosnia and HerzegovinaBulgariaCroatiaCyprusCzech RepublicDenmarkEstoniaFinlandFranceGeorgiaGermanyGreeceHungaryIcelandIrelandItalyKazakhstanKosovoLatviaLiechtensteinLithuaniaLuxembourgMaltaMoldovaMonacoMontenegroNetherlandsNorth MacedoniaNorwayPolandPortugalRomaniaRussiaSan MarinoSerbiaSlovakiaSloveniaSpainSwedenSwitzerlandTurkeyUkraineUnited KingdomVatican City Breadcrumb - - Federated Demonstrators Federated Demonstrators This page provides information on the research question coming from multiple European project that have been addressed using the PHIRI methodology for federated analysis which allows sensitive data to be mobilized to respond multiple research query in multiple sites, while preserving GDPR principles. The us case focus on: Vulnerable populations, inequality and risk factor with direct or indirect impact on COVID-19 outcome Delayed care in cancer patient Effects of the COVID-19 pandemic on maternal and newborn health COVID-19 related change in population mental health COVID-19 vaccine(s) effectiveness in preventing SARS-CoV-2 infection Title Vulnerable populations, inequality and risk factor with direct or indirect impact on COVID-19 outcome Research question Has the COVID-19 pandemic changed existing pattern of non-COVID-19 health care utilisation and mortality for vulnerable population within and between countries? This is based around answering the indirect effect of the pandemic on population health. Cohort Any patient 18 year old or older, with a hospital episode with a main diagnosis of any of the condition included in the cohort definition (i.e. heart attack, stroke, hip or knee replacements, or severe trauma) from 2019-01-01 until today. Title Delayed care in cancer patient Research question Has there been any increase in surgical and/or co-adjuvant (i.e. radiotherapy, chemotherapy, inmunotherapy) treatment delay in elegible woman diagnosed of breast cancer, a a consequence of the COVID-19 crisis? Cohort Women, 18 year old or older, with a first diagnosis of breast cancer between 2017-01-01 until today. Title Effects of the COVID-19 pandemic on maternal and newborn health Research question Effects of the COVID-19 pandemic on maternal and newborn health Cohort All birth a defined within each data source locally between 2017-01-01 until today. All birth with a gestational age of 22 week or more or when gestational age is missing with a birthweight of 500 g or more. Title COVID-19 related change in population mental health Research question Has there been any increase in individual with mental health risk factor or mental disease, a a consequence of the COVID19 crisis? This case study will measure change in population mental health associated with the COVID-19 pandemic. Cohort Any patient 18 year old or older with a contact with the healthcare system between 2017-01-01 until 2020-12-31 due to a mental health condition (i.e. with a diagnosis of major depressive disorder, Other depresive disorders, or Anxiety. Title COVID-19 Vaccine(s) effectiveness in preventing SARS-CoV-2 infection Research question How effective have the SARS-CoV-2 vaccination programme been in preventing SARS-CoV-2 infections? Cohort All people eligible to be vaccinated (from 5 to 115 year old, included) or with, at least, one dose of a SARS-CoV-2 vaccine (any of the available brands) having or not a previous SARS-CoV-2 infection. 2024 - European Health Information Portal Version 2.0 (20230915.1) Main navigation Search Fulltext search You can use boolean operator like AND, OR and NOT (in capital letters) to narrow your search. These tool have been implemented and tested to support the development of a variety of study on the indirect effect of the COVID19 pandemic . Country InternationalCountry outside EuropeAlbaniaAndorraArmeniaAustriaAzerbaijanBelarusBelgiumBosnia and HerzegovinaBulgariaCroatiaCyprusCzech RepublicDenmarkEstoniaFinlandFranceGeorgiaGermanyGreeceHungaryIcelandIrelandItalyKazakhstanKosovoLatviaLiechtensteinLithuaniaLuxembourgMaltaMoldovaMonacoMontenegroNetherlandsNorth MacedoniaNorwayPolandPortugalRomaniaRussiaSan MarinoSerbiaSlovakiaSloveniaSpainSwedenSwitzerlandTurkeyUkraineUnited KingdomVatican City Breadcrumb - - Health Information System Assessments Health Information System Assessments Health information system (HIS) are infrastructure that involve the resources, stakeholders, activity and output that allow for evidence-based health policy making and population health monitoring. Assessments of HIS are important tool in promoting health equity, setting priority for capacity building, improving element of a national HIS and promoting cross-country exchange on what make up a functional HIS. The assessment are expected to: Provide opportunity for other country to learn from the experience that will be gained during the assessments, and build on these when assessing their own HIS/ HI data flows. Create opportunity for engagement and knowledge exchange with national stakeholder and authorities. Identify key recommendation for resilient HIS, and contribute to capacity building across Europe, reducing HI inequality within and between country How are these assessment organised? Different project have analyzed HIS through country visits, where a developed by the WHO Regional Office for Europe wa adapted to the specific circumstance of the evaluation. The purpose of the WHO HIS tool is to allow for rapid and comprehensive mapping of the main element of the HIS, and provide an analysis that national actor can use to improve their system, and other country can learn from to inform best practices.Each assessment included a preparatory desk report, interview with national (and regional) stakeholders, a final report including a one-pager describing the relevant aspect of a country's HIS, a SWOT analysis and SMART recommendations, and a follow-up stakeholder meeting. What project conducted HIS assessments? (2018 - 2021): InfAct wa the EU Joint Action on Health Information project funded by the European Commission. The mission of the project wa to build a strong EU health information system, and address health information inequality between country through HIS assessments. Within InFact, focused on HIS assessment. Learn more . (2020 - 2023): PHIRIsupports research across Europe through the identification, access, assessment and reuse of population health and non-health data to underpin public health policy decision on COVID-19 and future health crises. of PHIRI aim to map the HIS that monitor the effect of COVID-19 on population health, and ass the COVID-19 health information flow in country through virtual country visits. Virtual country visit were carried out in selected European country that are part of the PHIRI consortium. Download the one-pager on the COVID-19 Health Information System Assessments . (2021 - 2022): TEHDAS is a joint action project that help EU member state and the European Commission develop and promote concept for the secondary use of health data to benefit public health, research and innovation in Europe. of TEHDAS conducted 12 country visit to engage with national stakeholder and map country readiness to join the European Health Data Space (EHDS). See result of the country visits. (2023): This project support participating country to enhance and improve national IT system in an efficient and coordinated manner, with the objective to obtain the needed interoperability with HERAs IT platform. In country visits, the national landscape maturity towards supporting the EU interoperability with HERA's IT platform will be mapped. Outputs of the assessment InFact describing and supporting EU health information activity Creation of research infrastructure () that support use case PHIRI PHIRI Comprehensive report on HIS assessment provided to national stakeholder Publicly availableon country visits, which facilitate cross-country exchange on HIS strength and weakness TEHDAS on 12 different EU national HIS, including evaluation of the country readiness to enter the EHDS EU HIP Anticipated published one pager describing the national IT system of evaluated countries, and recommendation for compliance with HERAs IT standard Which country are part of this exercise? The InfAct assessment took place in 2019 and were performed in Norway, Serbia, Austria, Romania, Moldova, Latvia, Estonia, Lithuania and Belgium. The PHIRI assessment were performed in Austria, Belgium, Italy, Greece, Hungary, Ireland, Malta, the Netherlands, Norway and Portugal by the end of the project (November 2023). The TEHDAS assessment were performed between December 2021 and December 2022 in Belgium, Czech Republic, Denmark, Estonia, Finland, Germany, Hungary, Ireland, the Netherlands, Portugal, Slovenia and Sweden. Organised event on the assessment Online training for assessor and assessed country Workshopat European Public Health Conference 2022: and Pitch at the Rapid Exchange Forum Special Edition February 27 2023 Workshop at the World Congress on Public Health 2023 Would you like to have an assessment performed in your country? 2024 - European Health Information Portal Version 2.0 (20230915.1) Main navigation Search Fulltext search You can use boolean operator like AND, OR and NOT (in capital letters) to narrow your search. Country InternationalCountry outside EuropeAlbaniaAndorraArmeniaAustriaAzerbaijanBelarusBelgiumBosnia and HerzegovinaBulgariaCroatiaCyprusCzech RepublicDenmarkEstoniaFinlandFranceGeorgiaGermanyGreeceHungaryIcelandIrelandItalyKazakhstanKosovoLatviaLiechtensteinLithuaniaLuxembourgMaltaMoldovaMonacoMontenegroNetherlandsNorth MacedoniaNorwayPolandPortugalRomaniaRussiaSan MarinoSerbiaSlovakiaSloveniaSpainSwedenSwitzerlandTurkeyUkraineUnited KingdomVatican City Breadcrumb - Glossary Glossary This glossary wa created by the consortium partner of the European project with the aim of establishing agreed definition of commonly used term to harmonise the work of the project. The aim is that the glossary can also be used by other project working in similar areas. The glossary wa created through a series of glossary working group calls, during which each definition wa discussed and agreed upon. This is a living document that will be updated regularly with the addition of new term and modifications, if needed, of the term and definition currently there. For the source of the specific definitions, please check the original HealthyCloud listed below. Few termsare specific to the PHIRI's activity and are not part of the HealthyCloud glossary. Source: Irene Kesisoglou, Shona Cosgrove, Pascal Derycke, Petronille Bogaert, Annika Jacobsen, Marco Roos, Anna Niemeyer, Alicia Martinez Garcia, Adrian Thorogood, Petr Holub, Irene Schluender, Salvador Capella-Gutierrez, Juan Gonzalez Garcia, Celia Alvarez Romero, Teresa D'Altri, Amy Curwin, Laura Portell Silva, & Lidia Lpez Cuesta. (2022). Glossary of commonly used term in the field of health data research - developed by the EU project HealthyCloud (1.0). Zenodo. GLOSSARY Aggregated data: Aggregated data is pooled data. Statistical data about several individual that have been combined to show general trend or value within the data.Aggregated data are not necessarily anonymised data. Anonymisation: The processing of personal data in such a manner that the personal data can no longer be attributed to a specific data subject. Removing personally identifiable information, so a to definitively not allow the identification of the data subjects.The method used to anonymise the data are context dependent. Cloud: Network of computing facility providing remote data storage and processing service through the internet. Cloud computing: Paradigm for enabling network access to a scalable and elastic pool of shareable physical or virtual resource with administration on-demand. Comparative population health research: Comparisons of health status, determinant and service use across countries, and/or over time. Consent: An individual agreement e.g. to participate in research, undergo a healthcare procedure, to personal data processing. Within the context of personal data, the GDPR defines consent as: Any freely given, specific, informed and unambiguous indication of the data subject's wish by which he or she, by a statement or by a clear affirmative action, signifies agreement to the processing of personal data relating to him or her. Data:Discrete observation of attribute or event that carry little meaning when considered alone Data can be defined a the recorded factual material that is commonly accepted in the scientific community a information that is required to support research findings. Refers to any digital representation of acts, fact or information and any compilation of such acts, fact or information, including in the form of sound, visual or audiovisual recording. There are four major categorical type of data for where the data come from: observational; experimental; simulated and derived. Data is information available for processing. Data access: The processing of data by a data user, which wa provided by a data holder, in accordance with specific technical, legal, or organisational requirements, without necessarily implying the transmission or downloading of such data. Data access right: the ability, right or permission to act on data in a defined location. Data altruism: Consent by data subject to process personal data pertaining to them, or permission of other data holder to allow the use of their non-personal data without seeking a reward, for purpose of general interest, such a scientific research purpose or improving public services. Data centric health research computational infrastructure: This infrastructure provides data a a service. This infrastructure includes services, such a data visualisation, hosting and processing of data. In particular, it canprocess health-related sensitive data. Technological infrastructure for data analysis, exploitation and/or processing. Data controller: Under Regulation (EU) 2018/1725, a well a under the GDPR, the data controller is the party that, alone or jointly with others, determines the purpose and mean of the processing of personal data. The actual processing may be delegated to another party, called the data processor. The controller is responsible for the lawfulness of the processing, for the protection of the data, and respecting the right of the data subject. The controller is also the entity that receives request from data subject to exercise their rights. Data curator:A person who is responsible for the quality and FAIRness of the health-related data, and to make sure the value of the data is discovered and accessible. This role also considers the possibility of enriching data when increasing it quality. Importantly, data curator might play a role regarding being processors, e.g. responsible for the data at hand. Data discoverability: The ability or a mechanism to browse and locate available data relevant to a specific user purpose (e.g., research project) in a non-targeted search. Data is more discoverable if the data collection ha metadata and the metadata is publicly accessible. Discoverability is related to findability from the FAIR principles. Data model: In a distributed research infrastructure, data model are a formal description of data source (entities, their attribute and their relationships) and metadata specific to a scientific study, that are the basis for semantic interoperability, thus allowing reliable comparative research. Data governance: Assembly of policy and processes, coordination aspects, data usage and accessibility principle and data management procedure for a certain health data infrastructure to ensure legal compliance, consistency and good data quality throughout the different stage of the data life cycle. Data processor: According to Article 3 (12) of Regulation (EU) 2018/1725, a processor shall mean "a natural or legal person, public authority, agency or other body which process personal data on behalf of the controller." The essential element is therefore that the processor only act "on behalf of the controller" and thus only subject to his instructions.In some cases, the processor may choose not to process the data himself, but may have recourse to a subcontractor who process the data on his behalf. In practice, this will depend upon the processor agreement entered into with the controller. Data provider/holder: Any natural or legal person, which is an entity or a body in the health or care sector, or performing research in relation to these sectors, a well a European Union institutions, bodies, office and agency who ha the right or obligation, or theability to make available, including to register, provide, restrict access or exchange certain data. Data quality: The degree to which a set of inherent characteristic of data fulfills requirements.Notes: The requirement are defined by the purpose of the processing and hence data quality can be viewed in other word also a a fitness for purpose. The purpose can be any use of the data, including primary use or secondary use. For the purpose of data protection, data quality refers to a set of principle laid down in Article 5 of the GDPR and Article 4 of Regulation (EU) 2018/1725, namely: Lawfulness, fairness and transparency Purpose limitation Data minimisation Accuracy Storage limitation Integrity and confidentiality Data reuse: The most simple form of data reuse is using the same data in the same way more than once (i.e. starting with an original dataset, and drawing different research inferences). The data can also be repurposed and used for another intent (i.e. using data from health insurance registry for health monitoring, or for research). Data sharing: Provision of data by a data controller to a data user for the purpose of joint or individual use of the shared data, based on condition of use, directly or through an intermediary. Data subject: As defined in the GDPR, a data subject is a person who can be identified, directly or indirectly, in particular by reference to an identifier such a a name, an identification number, location data, an online identifier or to one or more factor specific to the physical, physiological, genetic, mental, economic, cultural or social identity of that natural person. Data user:A natural or legal person/organisation who ha lawful access to certain personal or non-personal data and is authorised to use that data for commercial or noncommercial purposes. Dataset: Collection of data that is represented in a particular form. Datasets will vary depending upon the type of intended use, and how the collecting organization ha decided to organize their data upon collection. Dataset is essentially a heterogeneous term that could be made up of any type of collection for any type of data. Data curator: A person who is responsible for the quality and FAIRness of the health-related data, and to make sure the value of the data is discovered and accessible. This role also considers the possibility of enriching data when increasing it quality. Importantly, data curator might play a role regarding being processors, e.g. responsible for the data at hand. Dataset catalogue: A collection of datasets descriptions, which is arranged in a systematic manner and consists of a user-oriented public part, where information concerning individual dataset parameter is accessible by electronic mean through an online portal. Data steward: A person who ha an administrative role; they do not really use the data. They create guideline to make data FAIR and advice on how to do it. Stewards might have direct responsibility on the data at hand (processors) or not. Distributed research infrastructure: A decentralized and organised network of resources. FAIR Data principles: Principles to define the Findability, Accessibility, Interoperability, and Reuse of resource for human and computer at the source. For example, the principle emphasise machine-actionability (i.e., the capacity of computational system to find, access, interoperate, and reuse data with none or minimal human intervention) because human increasingly rely on computational support to deal with data a a result of the increase in volume, complexity, and creation speed of data. Findable: Data and supplementary material have sufficiently rich metadata and a unique and persistent identifier. Accessible: Metadata and data are understandable to human and machines. Data is deposited in a trusted repository Interoperable: Metadata use a formal, accessible, shared, and broadly applicable language for knowledge representation. Re-usable: Data and collection have a clear usage license and provide accurate information on provenance. Federated data analysis: Federated data analysis describes an analysis that is performed on multiple (often geographically) separated datasets. During this analysis, the data is not exchanged and can stay, for example, behind a given institution firewall. Only the interim result of a local analysis are exchanged between the data-hosting sites). The aggregated non-identifiable result from each local analysis are pooled and returned to the data user. Federated database: Afederated database systemis a type of(DBMS), which transparently map multiple autonomousinto a singlefederated database. The constituentare interconnected via aand may be geographically decentralized. Federated learning: This is a specific case of federated data analysis, for machine learning purposes. It is a learning technique that allows user to collectively reap the benefit of shared model trained from rich data collections. The learning task is conducted across multiple separate site coordinated centrally. Each site ha a local training dataset which is never shared . Instead, each site computes an update to the current global model maintained centrally, and only this updated model is communicated Health data: Personal data related to the physical or mental health of a natural person, including the provision of health care services, which reveal information about his or her health status.Health data collection: A technical infrastructure that hold datasets, make datasets available for use, and organises data in a logical manner. The datasets may come from different sources, hospital and/or research institute from the same country (national data repositories) or different country (international data repositories). Data collection may also cover appropriate, subject-specific location where researcher can submit their data. Data collection may have specific requirement concerning subject or research domain; data reuse and access; file format and data structure; and the type of metadata that can be used. Minimal inclusion criteria: A digital platform that receives and store data It receives data from a single source and/or multiple source Allows discovery of the stored health data It must have control over the data stored Other possible characteristic of a data collection: It could have a specific thematic, data type that it collect (e.g. a particular disease, a particular data type: genomic data, clinical data, EHRs) It could be part of one or more overarching data hub It could generate data Health data hub: Minimal inclusion criteria: A digital technical infrastructure with the core mission of enabling health data sharing It provides health data from different source It allows discovery of health datasets It ha a metadata discovery service It ha a data accessibility mechanism in accordance with existing regulation It ha an authorization functionality, provided by the same Data Hub or by an external institution. Health information: All organised and contextualised data on population health and health service activity and performance, individual or aggregated, that improves health promotion, prevention, care and policy-making. Health information systems: A health information system is the total of resources, stakeholders, activity and output enabling evidence-informed health policy-making. The health information system manages all type of health data, from EHRs to imaging data and population health data. HIS activity include: data collection, interpretation (analysis and synthesis), health reporting, and knowledge translation, i.e. stimulating and enhancing the uptake of health information into policy and practice. Health information system governance relates to the mechanism and process to coordinate and steer all element of a health information system. : An infodemic is an overabundance of information some accurate and some not that occurs during an epidemic. It spread between human in a similar manner to an epidemic, via digital and physical information systems. It make it hard for people to find trustworthy source and reliable guidance when they need it. Information: Data which is contextualised, i.e. reduced, summarized and adjusted for variation such a the age and sex of population so that comparison over time and place are possible. Infrastructure provider: The responsible organisation to support the physical management of health-related data following existing regulations. Parent definition for data hub, data collection and secure processing environment. Input Data: Data provided to or directly acquired by an AI system on the basis of which the system produce an output. Intelligence: the product of information being transformed through integration and processing with experience and perception based on social and political values. Interoperability: Following the European Interoperability Framework, interoperability refers to a) a full compliance with the legal and ethical provision in each constituent node; b) an organisation that support knowledge exchange and software transference across nodes; c) a compatible technological environment that support the communication between node and allows the deployment of the computational tasks; and d) the existence of common data model that enables semantic standardisation across data sources. In a distributed research infrastructure, interoperability is a key feature for it governance and achievements. Knowledge translation: The appropriate exchange, synthesis and ethically sound application of knowledge to intervention that strengthen the healthcare system and improve health. Machine learning: A subset of AI technique based on the use of statistical and mathematical modelling technique to define and analyse data. Such learned pattern are then applied to perform or guide certain task and make predictions. Metadata: A set of data that defines and describes a resource (e.g., data, dataset, sample...) so that it can be understood, discovered and reused. There are different level of metadata. Since metadata can be used to describe different aspect of data, we can group metadata property in term of quality, availability, provenance, processing, among others. Then there are metadata catalogue that can be developed to describe the available data collection in a repository or hub. Metadata is important to make data understandable, and can contribute to increase the findability, accessibility, interoperability and reusability of the data. Metadata can be collected or compiled in repository to improve the FAIRness level of the data collections. Mock-up data: Low quality synthetic data that do not have pattern such a correlation between variable (i.e social factor depending of area). Mock-up data can be used to know how the real data look like, or to create analysis script. However, they cannot be used to make real analysis (machine learning) a they do not reflect well the real data*. National Node: ANational Node (NN) is an organisational entity, often linked to a national institution or governmental unit that function a a national liaison and brings together relevant national stakeholder in the country in a systematic way. The relevant stakeholder may include, for example, the national statistical office, the national public health institutes, representative from ministry of health, research and/or science, and others. In addition, the NN may function a a discussion and advisory forum in matter of health data and information both for national or international matters. Examples include aspect of the governance of data, indicator and health reporting at the international level and health information stakeholder at national level. Non-personal data: All data other than personal data. Open data: Data that is freely available to everyone to use and republish a they wish, without restriction from copyright, patent or other mechanism of control. Open license is a license agreement which contains provision that allow other individual to reuse another creator's work, giving them four major freedoms. Without a special license, these us are normally prohibited by copyright law or commercial license. Most free license are worldwide, royalty-free, non-exclusive, and perpetual (see copyright durations). Free license are often the basis of crowdsourcing and crowdfunding projects. Open science: The movement to make scientific research (including publications, data, physical samples, and software) and it dissemination accessible to all level of an inquiring society, amateur or professional. Open science is transparent and accessible knowledge that is shared and developed through collaborative networks. It encompasses practice such a publishing open research, campaigning for open access, encouraging scientist to practice open-notebook science, and generally making it easier to publish and communicate scientific knowledge. Personal data:According to Article 3 (1) of Regulation (EU) 2018/1725: "personal data mean any information relating to an identified or identifiable natural person (data subject); an identifiable natural person is one who can be identified, directly or indirectly, in particular by reference to an identifier such a a name, an identification number, location data, an online identifier or to one or more factor specific to the physical, physiological, genetic, mental, economic, cultural or social identity of that natural person".Name and the social security number are two example of personal data which relate directly to a person. However, the definition extends further and also encompasses for instance e-mail address and the office phone number of an employee. Other example of personal data can be found in information on physical disabilities, in medical record and in an employee's evaluation. Personal data which is processed in relation to the work of the data subject remain personal/individual in the sense that they continue to be protected by the relevant data protection legislation, which strives to protect the privacy and integrity of natural persons. As a consequence, data protection legislation doe not address the situation of legal person (apart from the exceptional case where information on a legal person also relates to a physical person). Personal data breach: A breach of security leading to the accidental or unlawful destruction, loss, alteration, unauthorised disclosure of, or access to, personal data transmitted, stored or otherwise processed. Population Health Data/Health information: All organised and contextualised data on health and health service activity and performance, at individual or population level, that is fit-for-use and contributes to health promotion, prevention, care and policy-making. Primary use of data: The use of any data for the purpose for which it wa originally collected. Processing (personal and non-personal): Any operation or set of operation which is performed on data or on datasets, whether or not by automated means, such a collection, recording, organisation, structuring, storage, adaptation or alteration, retrieval, consultation, use, disclosureby transmission, dissemination or otherwise making available, alignment or combination, restriction, erasure or destruction. Profiling: Any form of automated processing of personal data consisting of the use of personal data to evaluate certain personal aspect relating to a natural person, in particular to analyse or predict aspect concerning that natural person's performance at work, economic situation, health, personal preferences, interests, reliability, behaviour, location or movements. Pseudonymisation: The processing of personal data in such a manner that the personal data can no longer be attributed to a specific data subject without the use of additional information, provided that such additional information is kept separately and is subject to technical and organisational measure to ensure that the personal data are not attributed to an identified or identifiable natural person. Public health monitoring and reporting: The activity necessary to obtain health data and information and bring this information into health policy and practice. Research Network: A Research Network (RN) is an active networkof national and/or regional expert from several country that perform comparative research in a specific health area (information domain). Restriction of processing (personal and non-personal data): As defined by the GDPR, method by which to restrict the processing of data could include, inter alia, temporarily moving the selected data to another processing system, making the selected personal data unavailable to users, or temporarily removing published data from a website. In automated filing systems, the restriction of processing should in principle be ensured by technical mean in such a manner that the personal data are not subject to further processing operation and cannot be changed. The fact that the processing of data is restricted should be clearly indicated in the system. Secondary use of data/data re-use:Secondary use refers to using data for a different purpose than the one it wa originally collected for (i.e. than the primary use). According to the European Data Governance Act 2020 re-use mean the use by natural or legal person of data held by public sector bodies, for commercial or noncommercial purpose other than the initial purpose within the public task for which the data were produced, except for the exchange of data between public sector body purely in pursuit of their public tasks. Clinical definition: Secondary use of health data applies personal health information (PHI) for us outside of direct health care delivery. Secure processing environment: The physical or virtual environment and organisational mean to provide the opportunity to re-use data in a manner that allows for the operator of the secure processing environment to determine and supervise all data processing actions, including to display, storage, download, export of the data and calculation of derivative data through computational algorithms. Sensitive data: Information that is regulated by law due to possible risk for plants, animals, individual and/or community and for public and private organisations. Sensitive personal data include information related to racial or ethnic origin, political opinions, religious or philosophical beliefs, trade union membership and data concerning the health or sex life of an individual. These data that could be identifiable and potentially cause harm through their disclosure. Synthetic data:The concept of synthetic data generation is to take an original data source (dataset) and create new, artificial data, with similar statistical property from it. Keeping the statistical property mean that anyone analysing the synthetic data, a data analyst for example, should be able to draw the same statistical conclusion from the analysis of a given dataset of synthetic data a he/she would if given the real (original) data. The use of synthetic data is growing in many fields: from training of artificial intelligence model within the health sector to computer vision, image recognition and robotics fields. *Synthetic data should not be confused with "mockup data", which, although close, is not synonymous. Mockup data is primarily used for initial testing purposes, e.g. in design phase to prototype applications. It doe not necessarily maintain the statistical property of real data. Learn more about the difference between synthethic v mockup data . Testing Data: Data used for providing an independent evaluation of the trained and validated AI system in order to confirm the expected performance of that system before it placing on the market or putting into service. Training Data: Data used for training machine learning algorithm (e.g., an artificial intelligence (AI) system) through fitting it learnable parameters. Validation Data: Data used for providing an evaluation of the trained AI system and for tuning it non-learnable parameter and it learning process. Use case: A software and system engineering term that describes how a userinteracts within a system to accomplish a particular goal. Ause caseacts a a software modeling technique that defines the feature to be implemented and the resolution of any error that may be encountered. *= Definitions not part of the HealthyCloud Glossary 2024 - European Health Information Portal Version 2.0 (20230915.1) Main navigation Search Fulltext search You can use boolean operator like AND, OR and NOT (in capital letters) to narrow your search.
